0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003epnpm uses a content-addressable filesystem to store all files from all module directories on a disk.\nWhen using npm, if you have 100 projects using lodash, you will have 100 copies of lodash on disk.\nWith pnpm, lodash will be stored in a content-addressable storage, so:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003col dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eIf you depend on different versions of lodash, only the files that differ are added to the store.\nIf lodash has 100 files, and a new version has a change only in one of those files,\n\u003ccode\u003epnpm update\u003c/code\u003e will only add 1 new file to the storage.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eAll the files are saved in a single place on the disk. When packages are installed, their files are linked\nfrom that single place consuming no additional disk space. Linking is performed using either hard-links or reflinks (copy-on-write).\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAs a result, you save gigabytes of space on your disk and you have a lot faster installations!\nIf you'd like more details about the unique \u003ccode\u003enode_modules\u003c/code\u003e structure that pnpm creates and\nwhy it works fine with the Node.js ecosystem, read this small article: \u003ca href=\"https://pnpm.io/blog/2020/05/27/flat-node-modules-is-not-the-only-way\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003eFlat node_modules is not the only way\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e💖 Like this project? Let people know with a \u003ca href=\"https://r.pnpm.io/tweet\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003etweet\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" <p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer nofollow" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/49b19604911bc6ee19d5e805bfcc525af7fdd3573f6449b1bd14454cc5aa48bc/68747470733a2f2f692e696d6775722e636f6d2f716c57316545472e706e67"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/49b19604911bc6ee19d5e805bfcc525af7fdd3573f6449b1bd14454cc5aa48bc/68747470733a2f2f692e696d6775722e636f6d2f716c57316545472e706e67" alt="" data-canonical-src="https://i.imgur.com/qlW1eEG.png" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto">Fast, disk space efficient package manager:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>Fast.</strong> Up to 2x faster than the alternatives (see <a href="#benchmark">benchmark</a>).</li>
<li><strong>Efficient.</strong> Files inside <code>node_modules</code> are linked from a single content-addressable storage.</li>
<li><strong><a href="https://pnpm.io/workspaces" rel="nofollow">Great for monorepos</a>.</strong></li>
<li><strong>Strict.</strong> A package can access only dependencies that are specified in its <code>package.json</code>.</li>
<li><strong>Deterministic.</strong> Has a lockfile called <code>pnpm-lock.yaml</code>.</li>
<li><strong>Works as a Node.js version manager.</strong> See <a href="https://pnpm.io/cli/env" rel="nofollow">pnpm env use</a>.</li>
<li><strong>Works everywhere.</strong> Supports Windows, Linux, and macOS.</li>
<li><strong>Battle-tested.</strong> Used in production by teams of <a href="https://pnpm.io/users" rel="nofollow">all sizes</a> since 2016.</li>
<li><a href="https://pnpm.io/feature-comparison" rel="nofollow">See the full feature comparison with npm and Yarn</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">To quote the <a href="https://rushjs.io/" rel="nofollow">Rush</a> team:</p>
<blockquote>
<p dir="auto">Microsoft uses pnpm in Rush repos with hundreds of projects and hundreds of PRs per day, and we’ve found it to be very fast and reliable.</p>
</blockquote>

<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Background</h2><a id="user-content-background" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Background" href="#background"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">pnpm uses a content-addressable filesystem to store all files from all module directories on a disk.
When using npm, if you have 100 projects using lodash, you will have 100 copies of lodash on disk.
With pnpm, lodash will be stored in a content-addressable storage, so:</p>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>If you depend on different versions of lodash, only the files that differ are added to the store.
If lodash has 100 files, and a new version has a change only in one of those files,
<code>pnpm update</code> will only add 1 new file to the storage.</li>
<li>All the files are saved in a single place on the disk. When packages are installed, their files are linked
from that single place consuming no additional disk space. Linking is performed using either hard-links or reflinks (copy-on-write).</li>
</ol>
<p dir="auto">As a result, you save gigabytes of space on your disk and you have a lot faster installations!
If you'd like more details about the unique <code>node_modules</code> structure that pnpm creates and
why it works fine with the Node.js ecosystem, read this small article: <a href="https://pnpm.io/blog/2020/05/27/flat-node-modules-is-not-the-only-way" rel="nofollow">Flat node_modules is not the only way</a>.</p>
<p dir="auto">💖 Like this project? Let people know with a <a href="https://r.pnpm.io/tweet" rel="nofollow">tweet</a></p>

<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Benchmark</h2><a id="user-content-benchmark" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Benchmark" href="#benchmark"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">pnpm is up to 2x faster than npm and Yarn classic. See all benchmarks <a href="https://r.pnpm.io/benchmarks" rel="nofollow">here</a>.</p>
